Note that we do not call\\n16:   // `clear()` here to avoid doing a deferred delete. This triggers some unwanted race conditions\\n17:   // on shutdown where deleted resources end up putting stuff on the deferred delete list after the\\n18:   // worker threads have shut down.\\n19:   clearActivePools();\\n20: }\\n21: \\n22: template <typename KEY_TYPE, typename POOL_TYPE>\\n23: typename ConnPoolMap<KEY_TYPE, POOL_TYPE>::PoolOptRef\\n24: ConnPoolMap<KEY_TYPE, POOL_TYPE>::getPool(const KEY_TYPE& key, const PoolFactory& factory) {\\n25:   Common::AutoDebugRecursionChecker assert_not_in(recursion_checker_);\\n26:   // TODO(klarose): Consider how we will change the connection pool's configuration in the future.\\n27:   // The plan is to change the downstream socket options... We may want to take those as a parameter\\n28:   // here. Maybe we'll pass them to the factory function?\\n29:   auto pool_iter = active_pools_.find(key);\\n30:   if (pool_iter != active_pools_.end()) {\\n31:     return std::ref(*(pool_iter->second));\\n32:   }\\n33:   ResourceLimit& connPoolResource = host_->cluster().resourceManager(priority_).connectionPools();\\n34:   // We need a new pool. How can we prevent iterating over all\\n46:     // pools when we're at the limit every time we want to allocate a new one, even if most of the\\n47:     // pools are not busy, while balancing that with not unnecessarily freeing all pools? If we\\n48:     // start freeing once we cross a threshold, then stop after we cross another, we could\\n49:     // achieve that balance.\\n50:   }\\n51: \\n52:   // We have room for a new pool. Allocate one and let it know about any cached callbacks.\\n53:   auto new_pool = factory();\\n54:   connPoolResource.inc();\\n55:   for (const auto& cb : cached_callbacks_) {\\n56:     new_pool->addIdleCallback(cb);\\n57:   }\\n58: \\n59:   auto inserted = active_pools_.emplace(key, std::move(new_pool));\\n60:   return std::ref(*inserted.first->second);\\n61: }\\n62: \\n63: template <typename KEY_TYPE, typename POOL_TYPE>\\n64: bool ConnPoolMap<KEY_TYPE, POOL_TYPE>::erasePool(const KEY_TYPE& key) {\\n65:   Common::AutoDebugRecursionChecker assert_not_in(recursion_checker_);\\n66: If no idle pool can be freed and the limit is reached, it increments the `upstream_cx_pool_overflow_` counter and returns an error.\\n\\n### Counter Definitions\\nThe counters tracking overflow are defined in **envoy/upstream/upstream.h** (line 726):\\n- `upstream_cx_pool_overflow`: Total times the cluster's connection pool circuit breaker overflowed\\n- `upstream_rq_pending_overflow`: Total times pending requests exceeded the configured limit\\n- `upstream_cx_overflow`: Total connection circuit breaker overflows (separate from pool overflow)\\n\\n### HTTP and TCP Implementation\\n**source/common/http/conn_pool_base.h** (lines 85-91) and **source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc** provide the HTTP-specific implementation of `onPoolFailure()`, which extracts the callback from the HTTP attach context and invokes it with the pool failure reason.\\n\\n**source/common/tcp/conn_pool.cc** provides the TCP implementation of the connection pool, inheriting the overflow handling from the base class.\\n\\n### Proxy Filters\\nBoth TCP and UDP proxies explicitly handle overflow conditions:\\n- **source/common/tcp_proxy/tcp_proxy.cc** (line 686): Increments `upstream_cx_overflow_` when a TCP connection cannot be established due to resource constraints.\\n- **source/extensions/filters/udp/udp_proxy/udp_proxy_filter.cc** (lines 823, 1044): Increments `upstream_cx_overflow_` when UDP sessions hit the session circuit breaker.\\n\\n### Summary\\nThe upstream connection pool overflow is a sophisticated resource management mechanism that prevents exhaustion of connection resources. The overflow state is defined centrally in `PoolFailureReason`, triggered through multiple resource limit checks in `ConnPoolImplBase::newStreamImpl()` and `ConnPoolImplBase::attachStreamToClient()`, and tracked through counters in the cluster traffic statistics. The mechanism propagates through protocol-specific implementations (HTTP, TCP, UDP) and is observable via Envoy metrics like `upstream_cx_pool_overflow`, `upstream_rq_pending_overflow`, and `upstream_cx_overflow`.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
